- Access to Gemini Pro, Google’s top AI model

[03/01/2026, 13:47:53] ~ Teo Forés Requena: TEDxVU Student Pitch Night
 	
We are happy to inform you that there is still time to register for the TEDx Student Pitch Night! Do you want the opportunity to become a TEDx speaker? Then this is your chance 🎙️

The goal of the Student Pitch Night is to find a creative and highly-driven student who can present alongside other speakers during the main TEDxVU event with this year's theme, “The Cycle”, which explores the rhythms, patterns and evolving loops that shape our world. In a time defined by rapid innovation and global uncertainty, The Cycle invites us to reflect on how change really happens: gradually, repeatedly and often only visible in hindsight. Amsterdam offers a meaningful lens for this exploration, as its bicycles, canals, tides and seasons create a living balance between movement and equilibrium, allowing a centuries-old city to continually reinvent itself through research, innovation, sustainability and collaboration.

Does this spark your interest? Then sign up now ✏️

📅 When: 15th of January 2026, 19:30
📍 Where: Vrije Universiteit Amsterdam, Agora • 2 (HG)
👥 Who: All VU students
🎙️ What: Five minute pitch about a personally chosen topic

If you are interested in attending, click here to register: https://forms.gle/NLHtZhbRVtDu9nRJ6

Kind Regards,
TEDxVU Committee 💛

[09/02/2026, 13:25:31] ~ Jakub Liška: Hey guys, i thought i might share an exercise that i prompted and that i find it useful to practice on:

Mega Exercise — CSV + Cleaning + Errors + Queries (10 methods)

This is a Part B–style “from scratch” coding task, but broader and harder. It’s designed to force you to demonstrate the full toolkit: parsing, validation, dedup, filtering, aggregation, exception handling, and writing output.

Data: events.csv

Header included:

EventID,UserID,Category,DurationMin,Date
E1,U10,study,45,2025-01-10
E2,U10,sleep,480,2025-01-10
E3,U11,study,not_a_number,2025-01-11
E4, ,work,60,2025-01-11
E5,U12,travel,30,2025-13-01
E6,U10,study,45,2025-01-10
E7,U11,work,120,2025-01-11
E8,U12,sleep,420,2025-01-12

Validation rules

A row is valid only if:
	•	EventID, UserID, Category, Date are non-empty after stripping
	•	DurationMin can be parsed as int and is > 0
	•	Date must be exactly format YYYY-MM-DD and represent a valid month/day
	•	You must validate it without importing datetime
	•	Accept months 1–12 and days 1–31 (no need for leap year logic)
	•	Dedup rule: ignore any later row with the same (EventID) (EventID must be unique)

Invalid rows are skipped silently.

File-not-found behavior: let FileNotFoundError be raised.

⸻

Your tasks

Task 1 — Class Event (6 pts)

Attributes:
	•	event_id: str
	•	user_id: str
	•	category: str
	•	duration_min: int
	•	date: str

__str__ must return:
"<event_id> <user_id> <category> <duration_min> <date>"

⸻

Task 2 — Class EventLog (44 pts)

Holds a list of Event objects.

Implement exactly these 10 methods:
	1.	add_event(self, event: Event) -> None
	2.	load_from_csv(self, path: str) -> int

	•	Loads valid events, applies all validation + dedup by EventID
	•	Returns the number of valid events added

	3.	count_invalid_rows(self, path: str) -> int

	•	Reads the file and returns number of invalid rows according to rules
	•	Must NOT modify self.events

	4.	get_by_user(self, user_id: str) -> list[Event]

	•	Exact match

	5.	get_by_category(self, category: str) -> list[Event]

	•	Exact match

	6.	total_duration_by_user(self, user_id: str) -> int

	•	Sum of durations for that user (0 if none)

	7.	most_common_category(self) -> str

	•	Return the category with highest count
	•	If no events, return ""
	•	Tie-break: if equal counts, return the category that is alphabetically smallest

	8.	daily_total(self, date: str) -> int

	•	Total duration for that date (0 if none)

	9.	export_user_summary(self, user_id: str, path: str) -> None

	•	Writes a CSV file with header:
Category,TotalDurationMin
	•	One row per category for that user, sorted by category alphabetically
	•	If user has no events, still write only the header

	10.	remove_user(self, user_id: str) -> int

	•	Removes all events for that user (in-place)
	•	Returns number removed

⸻

Tests (do not modify)

log = EventLog()
added = log.load_from_csv("events.csv")
print("added", added)

print("invalid", log.count_invalid_rows("events.csv"))

print("u10_total", log.total_duration_by_user("U10"))
print("study_count", len(log.get_by_category("study")))
print("common", log.most_common_category())
print("day", log.daily_total("2025-01-10"))

removed = log.remove_user("U11")
print("removed", removed)
print("u11_total", log.total_duration_by_user("U11"))

log.export_user_summary("U10", "u10_summary.csv")

Expected printed output (exact)

added 5
invalid 3
u10_total 525
study_count 2
common sleep
day 525
removed 1
u11_total 0

Notes:
	•	Valid events added should be: E1, E2, E6, E7, E8 (E6 is not a duplicate EventID, so it counts; only duplicates by EventID, not by content.)
	•	Invalid rows: E3 (bad duration), E4 (missing UserID), E5 (bad month)
